{"nick":"Lope","message":"weiwae: the common thread with the misunderstandings (according to my perception which may be wrong) is that you're not grasping the practical SCOPE OF ASYNC/SYNC. It's all about scope. It seems you've been looking at building blocks in isolation and then trying to label stuff async or sync, based on that. But that's not the way to think about things. It's important to consider the objectives, and how the code will run, then you can label something sync or a","date":"2016-08-08T11:45:28.897Z","type":"message"}
{"nick":"Lope","message":"sync, based on that. So what I'm saying is. If you use async building blocks to transform an input array to an output array, but the values can only be retrieved consecutively, then the entire algorithm must be labelled \"sync\". On the otherhand, contrastingly, you can use a synchronous thing like a for loop, which fires off asynchronous functions, which return \"immediately\" and perform async work in the background, and return their values via some async meth","date":"2016-08-08T11:45:29.181Z","type":"message"}
{"nick":"Lope","message":"od like promises or callbacks, then you can label the entire algo \"async\". So you see it doesn't matter if you use for, yield, whatever. It's how the whole thing runs that counts.","date":"2016-08-08T11:45:29.466Z","type":"message"}
